  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>It is a bit tricky to use EMMA to measure code coverage for the derby testing.</p> 
                  <p>Modifications must be made to the source both to avoid problems with the SecurityManager and individual tests. It would be good if these modifcations could be done once and for all so that it was easier for anyone to run the tests with EMMA.</p> 
                  <p>It would also be good to have ant tasks that would make it even easier to run the tests with EMMA.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

This is used in the policy files to grant permissions to emma.jar, without having to know where it will be placed by the person running the test.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eSeveral new tasks are added to build.xml for running tests with EMMA. The most important one is emma-report, which instruments your jar-files and places the instrumented copies under jars\\/emma\\/, and then runs the junit task &lt;junit-all&gt; before it creates three sets of coverage reports (txt, xml and html) linked to the derby source files. I\'ve adapted the old &lt;junit-all&gt; task to work with EMMA and ant 1.7.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAdded properties for emma.jar and emma_ant.jar in tools\\/ant\\/extrapath.properties. These changes are:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eExtra permissions in SecurityPolicyReloadingTest.initial.policy, NetworkServerControlApiTest.policy and ServerPropertiesTest.policy to get these tests to run with EMMA and ant 1.7.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAdded emma.jar to classpath for classloader used in SysinfoLocaleTest.java.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAdded property emma.verbosity.level=silent to commandline used in SecureServerTest.java.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis is a first step to make it easier to run with EMMA. The changes in this patch are: \\n \\n\\t A lot of new permissions in derby_tests.policy, both for EMMA writing to its coverage.ec file, and for running junit from ant with ant version 1.7 which writes to some temporary files. \\n\\t SecurityManagerSetup now sets a new property \\\"derbyTesting.emma\\\" to the location of emma.jar. If you \\n \\n\\n\\n I have made some test-specific changes as well, and put them in a separate pathfile named 3445-testspecific-diff. These changes are: \\n \\n\\t Extra permissions in SecurityPolicyReloadingTest.initial.policy, NetworkServerControlApiTest.policy and ServerPropertiesTest.policy to get these tests to run with EMMA and ant 1.7. \\n\\t Added emma.jar to classpath for classloader used in SysinfoLocaleTest.java. \\n\\t Added property emma.verbosity.level=silent to commandline used in SecureServerTest.java. \\n \\n\\n\\n\\n This is a first step to make it easier to run with EMMA. Going forward, it might be useful to improve the emma-tasks in build.xml to be able to run codecoverage experiments with the classes in addition to the jars and to integrate with the other junit-tasks \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI haven\'t found any problems with this change and ant 1.6. My experience with ant 1.6 is that to get things to work you need to use one of the workarounds described here: \u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/ant.apache.org\\/faq.html#delegating-classloader-1.6:\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/ant.apache.org\\/faq.html#delegating-classloader-1.6:\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e   1.  put all external libraries you need in CLASSPATH as well this is not what you want, otherwise you wouldn\'t have found this FAQ entry.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   2. put all external libraries you need in ANT_HOME\\/lib or .ant\\/lib. This probably still isn\'t what you want, but you might reconsider the .ant\\/lib option.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   3. Always start Ant with the -lib command line switch and point to your external libraries (or the directories holding them).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   4. remove the class that loads the external library from the coreloader.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo, basically my change has no effect with ant 1.6, it neither helps nor harms as far as I can understand. I am able to test with ant 1.6 if I for instance use the -lib option with ant.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf you are using ant 1.7 with my patch you just need to have junit.jar under your tools\\/java\\/ directory where the ant properties expect it to be. My experience with ant 1.6 is that to get things to work you need to use one of the workarounds described here:  http:\\/\\/ant.apache.org\\/faq.html#delegating-classloader-1.6:  \\n\\n    1.  put all external libraries you need in CLASSPATH as well this is not what you want, otherwise you wouldn\'t have found this FAQ entry. \\n   2. put all external libraries you need in ANT_HOME\\/lib or .ant\\/lib. This probably still isn\'t what you want, but you might reconsider the .ant\\/lib option. \\n   3. Always start Ant with the -lib command line switch and point to your external libraries (or the directories holding them). \\n   4. remove the class that loads the external library from the coreloader. \\n\\n So, basically my change has no effect with ant 1.6, it neither helps nor harms as far as I can understand. I am able to test with ant 1.6 if I for instance use the -lib option with ant. \\n\\n If you are using ant 1.7 with my patch you just need to have junit.jar under your tools\\/java\\/ directory where the ant properties expect it to be. \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThank you all for the comments and suggestions, I\'ve added two more patches based on the feedback.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e3445-SysinfoLocaleTest-diff has a fix for the bug pointed out by Dan.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e3445-singletest-diff is a response to Thomas\' wish for a way to run a single test with EMMA using ant.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAdded a task &lt;junit-single&gt; which is in turn used by a task &lt;emma-single&gt;. Both need the property derby.junit.testclass set to some classname that will be attempted run as a junit test\\/suite.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo, doing: \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\\"ant emma-single -Dderby.junit.testclass=org.apache.derbyTesting.functionTests.tests.tools.SysinfoLocaleTest\\\" \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nshould run that particular test with codecoverage.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI also changed my use of ${junit} to ${javatools.dir}\\/junit.jar, as the first property is set in tools\\/ant\\/extrapath.properties and those properties are only loaded for compilation and not when just running a junit test.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ll write up some information on what you need to test with EMMA and how to use the new junit and emma targets, probably on monday. Both need the property derby.junit.testclass set to some classname that will be attempted run as a junit test\\/suite. \\n \\n\\n\\n So, doing:  \\n\\\"ant emma-single -Dderby.junit.testclass=org.apache.derbyTesting.functionTests.tests.tools.SysinfoLocaleTest\\\"  \\nshould run that particular test with codecoverage. \\n\\n I also changed my use of ${junit} to ${javatools.dir}\\/junit.jar, as the first property is set in tools\\/ant\\/extrapath.properties and those properties are only loaded for compilation and not when just running a junit test. \\n\\n I\'ll write up some information on what you need to test with EMMA and how to use the new junit and emma targets, probably on monday. E.g. could add this policy file emma.policy:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&gt; \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&gt; grant codebase \\\"... path to emma jars\\\" \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{\\n&gt;    \\/\\/ permissions needed\\n&gt; }\\n\u003cp\u003e&gt; \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&gt; java -jar derbyrun.jar server -additionalPolicy emma.policy start\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&gt; \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&gt; This would then be logically added into the permission set that Derby installs automatically.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAs far as I understand your suggestion is to add a new option to the network server (-additionalPolicy, or something along those lines). This new option would then only have an effect if the network server is started in a way that causes it to install its own default security policy. The effect would then be to merge the contents of the default policy file (server.policy) with whatever policy file is added with the new argument (emma.policy) into a new file, and then set the java.security.policy property to point to this file before installing a SecurityManager. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWould this be a feature added just to be able to test the product with EMMA, or do you think of other use cases as well?\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nReal users would be able to put a policy file under ${user.home}\\/.java.policy or just set -Djava.security.policy, so I guess they wouldn\'t have a need for it. \u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"vemund\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12583713_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=vemund\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"vemund\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Vemund \\u00D8stgaard\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12583713_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'31\\/Mar\\/08 15:05\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-03-31T15:05:47+0000\'\u003e31\\/Mar\\/08 15:05\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    &gt; A better long term solution would be to allow a set of policies to be added into the network server\'s default set. E.g. could add this policy file emma.policy: \\n&gt;  \\n&gt; grant codebase \\\"... path to emma jars\\\"  \\n{\\n&gt;    \\/\\/ permissions needed\\n&gt; }\\n &gt;  \\n&gt; java -jar derbyrun.jar server -additionalPolicy emma.policy start \\n&gt;  \\n&gt; This would then be logically added into the permission set that Derby installs automatically. \\n\\n As far as I understand your suggestion is to add a new option to the network server (-additionalPolicy, or something along those lines). This new option would then only have an effect if the network server is started in a way that causes it to install its own default security policy. The effect would then be to merge the contents of the default policy file (server.policy) with whatever policy file is added with the new argument (emma.policy) into a new file, and then set the java.security.policy property to point to this file before installing a SecurityManager.  \\n\\n Would this be a feature added just to be able to test the product with EMMA, or do you think of other use cases as well? \\nReal users would be able to put a policy file under ${user.home}\\/.java.policy or just set -Djava.security.policy, so I guess they wouldn\'t have a need for it.
